Differential Resolution (DR) is a data-driven method to improve seismic resolution but it can introduce a false spatial amplitude variation in the seismic output due to whole trace normalisation. Newly proposed normalisation technique which decomposes the input seismic trace using a translating Gaussian window and then implements the DR algorithm on each window. The introduced weight factors give the interpreter control of the degree of spectral broadening. These developments enable the algorithm to account for the non-stationary properties of the seismic trace, reduce spurious spatial amplitude variation and provide broader bandwidth seismic for detailed analysis. <br style=\"box-sizing&#58;border-box;\">To further understand on NSDR, you may go to SEG Geophysics site&#58; class=\"ExternalClassCA2AF5CFEAE044348BC09DD3AF3D72B3\"><p>\u200bT-2-Z is a newly developed software to assist velocity model building and time to depth conversion. It is developed as continuation of the project &quot;Gas Cloud Depth Conversion for Post-Processed Data&quot; which was endorsed at TRL4 in July 2016. The project was initiated in order to enhance the previous in-house established techniques of time-to-depth conversion and to incorporate the correction of the effect of shallow gas cloud on the underlying horizons. Although the project is initially focused on gas-affected areas, the software created is generic and can be used for depth conversion wherever there are overburden velocity anomalies which have not been explicitly corrected for as part of the imaging process. Even when PSDM is used to correct an overburden velocity anomaly, converting the data back to time with the exact imaging velocity model will &quot;re-introduce&quot; the overburden time effects \u2013 therefore these will need to be incorporated back in the depth conversion model. To avoid this issue with PSDM, a time conversion can be made with a smooth velocity model which has the overburden effects removed. In this latter case the overburden effects can be considered as corrected in time, and a simple depth conversion can proceed to tie wells. The project was initiated in order to enhance the previous in-house established techniques of time-to-depth conversion and to incorporate the correction of the effect of shallow gas cloud on the underlying horizons. To avoid this issue with PSDM, a time conversion can be made with a smooth velocity model which has the overburden effects removed. In this latter case the overburden effects can be considered as corrected in time, and a simple depth conversion can proceed to tie wells. minimum noise boost.</p><p>High-resolution seismic data enables better well ties, structure delineation, stratigraphic mapping and reservoir characterisation. Differential Resolution (DR) is a data-driven method to improve seismic resolution but it can introduce a false spatial amplitude variation in the seismic output due to whole trace normalisation. Newly proposed normalisation technique which decomposes the input seismic trace using a translating Gaussian window and then implements the DR algorithm on each window. The introduced weight factors give the interpreter control of the degree of spectral broadening. These developments enable the algorithm to account for the non-stationary properties of the seismic trace, reduce spurious spatial amplitude variation and provide broader bandwidth seismic for class=\"ExternalClass2437577E8DC04894B9A882952161CA94\"><p>\u200bIn order to reach the target of Net Zero Carbon Emission (NZCE) by 2050, the Carbon Capture and Storage (CCS) is required to develop HC fields with high CO2 content. For storage part, robust integrated subsurface assessments and modeling of potential storage site are crucial to reduce uncertainty, mitigate risks and ensure long term and safe containment of CO2 in the subsurface. Integrated coupled modelling study is used to mature the storage site fields. </p><p style=\"text-align&#58;left;\">Current industry coupled modelling practice for CO<sub>2</sub> storage simulation studies is conducted individually (standalone) without interaction between geomechanics and geochemistry. The simulations are mostly covered between dynamic fluid flow + geomechanics or dynamic fluid flow + geochemistry. In PETRONAS, current CO<sub>2</sub> storage simulation studies are conducted individually using three different platforms (software) namely, Eclipse, TOUGHREACT and VISAGE. In addition, there is no internal guideline for fully coupled modelling simulation. Therefore, it is inadequate to describe the complex subsurface physical, rock mechanics and chemical interactions that will happen during CO<sub>2</sub> injection and after CO<sub>2</sub> injector wells shut in.</p><p style=\"text-align&#58;left;\">A fully integrated coupled model which allows 3-way coupled reservoir modelling (Geochemical-Dynamic-Geomechanics) and properties update such as pressure, porosity and permeability values at different time steps is required to ensure long term safety of CO<sub>2</sub> containment in reservoir without release of CO<sub>2</sub> to atmosphere. The numerical modelling is crucial, especially to simulate geochemical processes for the consequences of long-term CO<sub>2</sub> storage in formations because some minerals take a very long time to react so it cannot be experimentally accessible. </p><p style=\"text-align&#58;left;\">This integrated coupled modelling workflow and guidelines provide the coupled geomechanics, dynamic and geochemical modelling to address the maximum storage capacity, injection performance, caprock integrity, maximum fracture pressure limit, compaction-subsidence, CO2 trapping mechanism and long-term fate study.</p></div>","OData__ModerationStatus":0,"AverageRating":null,"RatingCount":null,"LikesCount":null,"InstallerType":"Not class=\"ExternalClass85507F2E430B4F4E8E97A45A628BEF1D\"><p>\u200bThe tool is able to predict breakout initiation, progression and stabilization. In the market, 1D MEM software are only able to predict the (elastic) width of the well breakout based on simple hoopstress comparison with UCS around the wellbore. The main underlying issue with 1D MEM is it is only able to provide the angle and the width of the wellbore damage. Being 1D solution, it is only depth and point based where equations are solved independent of one another. Hence, it is unable to determine the severity of the damage, i.e. severity and magnitude. Furthermore, elastic solution and analysis used are not representation of real world scenario. This may lead to inaccurate understanding of the actual wellbore behavior and causing over prediction in mud weight. Narrower and higher mud weight used in drilling could potentially damaging the formation.<br><br>Backed by rigorous and comprehensive experimental campaign with state of the art numerical finite element simulation, Our PETRONAS DWBS is able to do things that conventional 1D MEM cannot do, which is predict breakout initiation, progression and stabilization. This has provided a step change on what driller would be able to estimate and visualize their borehole condition before drilling the well. The novelty of the model is the quantitative prediction of stabilized breakout geometries in shales which will widen safe mud weight window and marking the beginning of an new era of pragmatic safe drilling operations with the aim to deliver strong improvement as compared to conventional method, transitioning from 1D and qualitative, to 3D with quantitative accuracy, in order to provide optimum drilling program, while reducing risks related to drilling Non Productive Time (NPT).<br><br>In the year 2017, the project has being awarded with the IET Innovation Award for the category of Model Based Engineering and also Henri-Doll SEA Reservoir Symposium for the dedication, resilience and innovation demonstrated by the project team during the ideation and development this new hypothesis on wellbore failure stabilization into a full-fledged, digital 3D simulation and prediction tool.</p></div>","OData__ModerationStatus":0,"AverageRating":5,"RatingCount":2,"LikesCount":null,"InstallerType":"Request","AppSupport":"<div class=\"ExternalClassA499C96EAA0F43D5A7B82E62B0EAC863\"><h3>\u200bOverview of FPC</h3><p>FPC is primarily designed to be used for reservoir surveillance &amp; monitoring, opportunity identification and forecasting. For surveillance &amp; monitoring, the strings' health check can be done anywhere, at any time using dataset that resides in PETRONAS Global Production System (PGPS).&#160; FPC can also be utilized by users to screen new opportunities for production enhancement and optimization.&#160; Most importantly, FPC can produce seamless production forecasting and shorten the time taken to estimate reserves for input to the Annual Review of Petroleum Resources (ARPR) report.</p><p dir=\"rtl\" style=\"text-align&#58;right;\">&#160;</p><h3>Technical Aspect of FPC</h3><p>The Field Performance Center (FPC) initiated in October 2015 by PED in collaboration with GTD was initially developed as a quick visualization tool to digitally showcase COB field status and production parameters at Petroleum Engineering Department floors in Tower 2.&#160; The FPC was deployed in December 2015 and later became part of the PETRONAS DIGITAL initiative that includes the Integrated Operations (IO). It was then enhanced and has evolved into a full-fledged surveillance, monitoring and forecasting tool that is now accessible to 500+ users, becoming the most widely used engineering application in PETRONAS and is also an enabler for Pro-active Surveillance.
